  make art
  --------
  festival of free art and technologies

  _in-between design:
  rediscovering collaboration in digital art_

  from 4 to 7 november 2010
  **Maison de l'Architecture, Poitiers**


  make art is an international festival dedicated to free/libre arts and
  technologies, distributed digital artworks and net art. The sixth edition of
  make art focuses on works halfway between art and design, collaborative,
  scalable and participative methods. The adventure "in-between design" begins
  here, to be imagined in this creative development, where everyone can
  participate and where artwork keeps on evolving. Are these projects just
  curiosities or a real alternative to the graphic conformism ruled by an
  industry that dictates its aesthetic codes? Please come and join us to answer
  this question...
  
  `./configure && make art`


% FROM: --> http://makeart.goto10.org/2010/?lang=en

% ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- %

% ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- %

  make art
  --------
  festival des arts et technologies libres
  
  _in-between design:
  la redécouverte de la collaboration dans les arts numériques_
  
  du 4 au 7 novembre 2010
  **Maison de l'Architecture, Poitiers**
  
  
  make art est un festival international dédié aux arts et technologies libres,
  aux oeuvres numériques distribuées et à l'art en réseau. La sixième édition de
  make art se penche sur les créations à mi-chemin entre art et design, aux
  méthodes participatives, évolutives et collaboratives. L'aventure "in-between
  design" débute ici, elle s'imagine dans ce développement créatif, où la
  participation de chacun est possible et où l'oeuvre ne cesse d'évoluer. Ces
  projets sont-ils juste des curiosités ou bien une véritable alternative au
  conformisme graphique régi par une industrie qui nous impose ses codes
  esthétiques ? Venez nous rejoindre pour répondre à cette question...
  
  `./configure && make art`


% FROM: --> http://makeart.goto10.org/2010/?lang=en

% ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- %
% ::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: %
% ----------------------------------------------------------------------------- %

  A [TRUNK](http://www.forkable.eu/generators/i-bd/i/TRUNK/) of
  graphics is split into elements and the cut-set is layouted according to
  the laws of physic. __Drop it like it's hot__!
  [Inkscape]()
  meets
  [GNU's Bourne-Again SHell](http://www.gnu.org/software/bash/)
  meets
  [Processing ](http://www.processing.org/)
  meets the
  [*Philosophiae Naturalis Principia Mathematica*](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophi%C3%A6_Naturalis_Principia_Mathematica).
  
  Thumbs up to
  [Ricard Marxer](http://www.ricardmarxer.com/)
  for
  [Fisica](http://www.ricardmarxer.com/fisica/)
  and
  [Geomerative](http://www.ricardmarxer.com/geomerative/).
  
  To solve the *colour-print-is-expensive* problem facing big
  generative print runs we used a offset/laser combination.
  
  
  [Explore the repository](http://www.forkable.eu/generators/i-bd)

  10h30-19h00 Exhibition
  11h00-15h00 « brunch club »

  ######################################################################
  ## II/ texts
  ######################################################################

  « In-between design: rediscovering collaboration in digital art »

  make art is an international festival dedicated to free/libre arts
  and technologies, distributed digital artworks and net art. The sixth
  edition of make art focuses on works halfway between art and design,
  collaborative, scalable and participative methods. The adventure
  "in-between design" begins here, imagined in this creative development,
  where everyone can participate and where artwork keeps on evolving.
  Are these projects just curiosities or a real alternative to the
  graphic conformism ruled by an industry that dictates its aesthetic
  codes? Please come and join us to answer this question...

  ./configure && make art



  EXHIBITION
  ==========

  "Nancy" - Open Source Publishing (Belgium) -- Come and participate in
  the creation of an ornament font! As a trainee typographer during the
  time of your visit to the exhibition, you will be called to contribute
  to Nancy, the collaborative characters font. How to? Just redraw the
  standard symbols of two fonts (Dingbats and Unicode Miscellaneous
  Symbols) as you wish. Using basic means, you can make your own
  creations, taking inspiration from symbols drawn in previous workshops
  or giving free rein to your imagination.

  "Sonobotanics" - Marije Baalman (Netherlands) -- Periperceptoida
  Triquetrus Nutandis and Periperceptoida Triquetrus Dependis have all the
  characteristics of a plant: roots, stem, buds, leaves and flowers... but
  they are actually small atypical electroacoustic creations. Their
  electronic sensors interpret touch, light, temperature, humidity,
  ambient sound and the audience presence. Once combined, these data
  define a metaphorical and sound environment for the sonobotanic
  plant growth.

  "Drawn Together" - Evan Raskob (United States) -- Lines, circles,
  squares, dots and various squiggles: these are simple forms for an
  intuitive and childlike drawing where the image you're composing is
  associated with a musical loop of a song. The images of your graphic
  tablet drawings are then put together with the ones of other visitors,
  which will make up an animated exquisite corpse style video clip.

  "Trademark_Electric_Painting" - Dave Young (Ireland) -- Coca Cola,
  Google, Amazon, Facebook, Shell, Microsoft... They rule our lives with
  their ubiquitous visual identity. With Trademark_Electric_Painting,
  the logos and colors of these big trademarks are dissected,
  deconstructed and continuously modified to become abstract electronic
  compositions. This new marketing grammar is a noisy-glitch delight!

  "Laptopograms" - Aditya Mandayam (India) -- Have you ever thought
  of producing silver images using the light sources of a mobile phone,
  television, laptop screen? This crafty idea takes the opposite course of
  the digital photography principle by updating the photogram principle, a
  photographic image produced without a camera or enlarger, and created by
  placing objects on photosensitive surface exposed to a light source. In
  the case of the laptopogram light source and objects are replaced by
  computer screens whose trace would later be revealed as a screen shot,
  in a literal sense.

  "Yeep!Eep!Eep!" - Daniel Temkin (United States) -- Yeep!Eep!Eep!Program
  (or YEEP) creates databent images using the unique retro pseudo-graphics
  of the Commodore 64. By manipulating the VIC registers, YEEP generates
  images based on data that happens to be in RAM at the time, and what
  was on the screen just before the program ran. This information is
  mediated through character sets controlled by the user. It also has
  controls to alter the color and add additional data to be drawn. The
  entire palette available on the C64 is in use (all 16 colors!).

  "Digital dump" - Loredana Bontempi (Italy) -- Ddump is an online
  digital dump, where you are invited to share your computer trashes and
  encouraged to take ownership of files left by previous owners. Playing
  with the recycling trends in contemporary design and with existing
  metaphors in graphical interfaces such as the desktop or the trash,
  ddump takes an unusual look at your "dumped" files by offering them
  a second life as raw material for designers and artists.

  "make art 2010" - LAFKON (Germany) -- Inkscape meets the Bash meets
  Processing meets the Philosophiae Naturalis Principia Mathematica.
  In plaintext. Glyphs and graphics enter the wonderful world of physics
  to become posters for make art 2010.
  Thumbs up for Ricard Marxer and his Fisica and Geomerative libraries.


  CONCERTS
  ========

  EXTRA VERNISSAGE - in collaboration with Jazz À Poitiers

  MCLD "CODEBOX" -- MCLD brings together for the first time two different
  improvisatory worlds: beatboxing and livecoding. Beats and bleeps and
  noises; all improvised. Come and see if it's even possible!

  ----

  PLANETARIUM - in collaboration with the Lieu Multiple

  doebereiner & morimoto (Germany+Japan), Jaime Oliver (Peru), Andrés
  Colubri (Argentina), Awkward Family Photos (Greece)

  In search of the unexplored, these artists communicate their
  visual and sound imagination and their relationship to technology
  by creating and playing their own instruments. By amplifying their
  gesture and increasing their sensitivity, they invite you to various
  trips: rough-textured microstructures compositions by döbereiner &
  morimoto, touch and digital lute-making with Jaime Oliver, fantasies
  and childhood memories with Andrés Colubri, fantastic landscapes with
  Awkward Family Photos.

  ----

  PLACARD - in collaboration with the Confort Moderne

  Benjamin Cadon "2013" (France), Marije Baalman "Code LiveCode Live"
  (Netherlands), Noish "Noish~ vs Automata_v001" (Spain), Alberto de Campo
  (Austria), Segmentation Fault (Spain)

  Every year make art encloses itself in a "placard" (cupboard in French)
  for one evening. It is a place dedicated to headphone listening only,
  where unusual sound and visual experimentations occur, at the crossroads
  of electronic, improvised and noise music. Come and join us in our
  "placard", we will make some room for you.
  Tonight Benjamin Cadon will reorchestrate and debug the famous
  blockbuster 2012 using micro-loops, Marije Baalman will livecode from
  her own livecoding performance (!), Noish~ vs Automata_v001 duo will
  grow an improvisation starting from seven sound seeds, Alberto de
  Campo will combine analog and digital meta-control to make a musical
  exploration on the fly, while Segmentation Fault will patch and merge
  drones with deconstructed rhythms.
  Limited numbers of headphones and pillows so don't be late or bring
  yours!

  ----

  LECTURES
  ========

  Outlooks

   * "Gambiarra and the prototyping perspective" Gabriel Menotti (Brazil)
   * "Remix it Yourself" Vito Campanelli (Italy)
   * "Brainch" <stdin> (France)
   * Yann Le Guennec (France) (to be confirmed)

  Workbench

   * "Digital dump" Loredana Bontempi (Italy)
   * "Peer-to-peer design strategies" Emanuele Bonetti (Italy)
   * "FLOSS issues in graphic design" Calcyum (France)
   * "Dingbat Liberation Fest 0.4" Open Source Publishing (Belgium)

  Savoir-faire

   * "Laptopograms" Aditya Mandayam (India)
   * "Varia Zoosystematica Profundorum" Alberto de Campo (Austria)
   * "objscrs/Kaleidoscope" Simon Yuill (United Kingdom) &
      Dorothé Depeauw (Belgium)
   * "Libre Graphics Magazine" Ginger Coons (Canada)

  "Brunch club"

  The brunch club is an exclusive combination of breakfast, lunch and
  panel discussions. The meal usually involves standard chatty breakfast
  foods such as annotated bibliographical eggs, discursive fruits,
  arguing pastries, confused pancakes, and the like. However, it can
  include almost any other type of food and topics served throughout
  the day or during the rest of the festival. Buffets may have academic
  quiche, critical salads, convincing soups, passionated vegetable dishes,
  many types of controversial breadstuffs, and suggestive desserts of
  all sorts.

  ----

  WORKSHOP
  ========

  Emanuele Bonetti "Peer-to-peer design strategies" (IT) --
  The project "Peer-to-peer design strategies" investigates new practical
  approaches to graphic design based on peer-to-peer collaboration. The
  aim is to complete graphic design products that all participants find
  satisfying and to find out whether peer-to-peer design methodologies
  can serve as a full alternative to the hierarchical top-down model
  that dominates the industry.

  « in-between design: rediscovering collaboration in digital art »
  
  make art is an international festival dedicated to free/libre arts
  and technologies, distributed digital artworks and net art. The sixth
  edition of make art focuses on works halfway between art and design,
  collaborative, scalable and participative methods. The adventure
  "in-between design" begins here, to be imagined in this creative
  development, where everyone can participate and where artwork keeps on
  evolving. Are these projects just curiosities or a real alternative to
  the graphic conformism ruled by an industry that dictates its aesthetic
  codes? Please come and join us to answer this question...
  
  with Awkward Family Photos (Greece), Marije Baalman (Netherlands), Emanuele
  Bonetti (Italy), Loredana Bontempi (Italy), Vito Campanelli (Italy), Benjamin
  Cadon (France), Calcyum (France), Alberto de Campo (Austria), Andrés Colubri

  make art est un festival international dédié aux arts et technologies

  sixième édition de make art se penche sur les créations à mi-chemin

  nous rejoindre pour répondre à cette question...

  *CALL FOR PROJECTS*
  
  The sixth edition of make art – in-between design: rediscovering
  collaboration in digital art – will take place in Poitiers (FR), from
  the 4th to the 7th of November 2010.
  
  make art is an international festival dedicated to the integration
  of Free/Libre/Open Source Software (FLOSS) in digital art.
  make art offers performances, presentations, workshops and an
  exhibition, focusing on the encounter between digital art and free
  software.
  
  
  *in-between design: rediscovering collaboration in digital art*
  
  Today's market production accelerates the spread of non-critical and
  standardized aesthetics, by means of locked top-down distribution
  mechanisms and a series of tools that enforce it. At the same time
  new forms of methodologies inspired or powered by free software,
  participatory practices and peer-to-peer networks are fueling many
  Internet subcultures. Some of these emerging practices will lead to
  competitive social productions, while other will remain as pure
  artistic experiments.
  
  By adopting production and distribution methods based on free software
  and open standards and by sharing the sources of one's work with
  others, the collective knowledge base and aesthetic sensibilities can
  freely interact to explore uncharted, hybrid directions which no
  longer reflect the supremacy of a single idea.
  
   - Does the sharing of artworks "recipes" and tools help debunk
     the myth of the isolated design genius?
   - By leaving the possibility of ongoing development and refinement,
     is it possible to ever produce a "final" design?
   - Can these methods and technologies inspire new forms of creation or
     tools, beyond self-referential productions?
   - Is it wishful thinking to approach collaborative graphical design
     in the same way as an open source software project?
   - Is Free and Open Source licensing a catalyst for creation or does
     it add an extra level of complexity?
   - Can the limitation of one license trigger new forms of constrained
     creativity?
  
  We're currently seeking new, innovative media art and design works and
  projects focusing on the above theme and questions:
   - graphical artworks and installations
   - lectures
   - project presentations
   - software and hardware demos
  
  We're also seeking audiovisual performances that will take place
  during the festival evenings.
  
  The submitted projects must fit this focus and be made in a free/libre
  and open source environment, this includes both its optional
  dependencies or production tools and the operating system. We are
  asking you to publish the sources of your project under a free culture
  license of your choice or release it into the public domain.
  Projects that do not meet these criteria will not be considered.
  
  
  *How to apply*
  
  Submission form and a list of additional requirements are available at:
  http://makeart.goto10.org/call/
  
  Deadline: *Saturday 31 July 2010*
  
  Incomplete or late applications will not be processed.
  
  
  *Timeline*
  
  31st of July 2010       – Deadline call for proposals
  Beginning of September  – Selected projects notifications
  4th-7th of November 10  – make art 2010 - Poitiers (FR)
  
  For examples of previous editions, please visit the archives :
  http://makeart.goto10.org/
  
  make art is powered by GOTO10
  
  -- 
  
  *APPEL A PROJETS*
  
  La sixième édition de make art – "in-between design" : la
  redécouverte de la collaboration en art numérique – se déroule à
  Poitiers (FR), du 4 au 7 novembre 2010.
  
  make art est un festival international dédié à l'intégration des
  Logiciels Libres et Open Source (FLOSS) dans l'art numérique.
  make art propose des performances, des présentations, des ateliers
  et une exposition, centrés sur la rencontre entre l'art numérique
  et le logiciel libre.
  
  
  *"in-between design" : la redécouverte de la collaboration en art numérique*
  
  La production de marché d'aujourd'hui accélère la diffusion
  d'esthétiques standardisées non critiques, au moyen de mécanismes
  de distribution "top-down" verrouillés et d'une série d'instruments
  pour la faire respecter. Parallèlement de nouvelles formes de
  méthodologies inspirées ou fonctionnant sur du logiciel libre, des
  pratiques participatives et des réseaux peer-to-peer alimentent de
  nombreuses sous-cultures Internet. Certaines de ces pratiques
  émergentes conduiront à des productions sociales compétitives,
  tandis que d'autres resteront de pures expériences artistiques.
  
  En adoptant des méthodes de production et de distribution
  basées sur du logiciel libre et des standard ouverts, en partageant
  les sources de ses travaux avec d'autres, les sensibilités
  esthétiques, les parcours et les connaissances de chacun vont
  pouvoir librement et collectivement explorer des horizons métissés
  inexplorés qui ne reflèteront plus la suprématie d'une seule idée.
  
   - Le partage des "recettes" des œuvres et des outils aidera-t-il à
     briser le mythe du génie du design isolé ?
   - En permettant un développement et d'un affinement continuels
     est-ce toujours possible de produire un design "final" ?
   - Ces méthodes et technologies peuvent-elles inspirer de nouvelles
     formes de création ou d'outils, qui dépassent les productions
     auto-référentes ?
   - Est-ce utopique d'aborder le design graphique collaboratif de la
     même manière qu'un projet de logiciel open source ?
   - L'utilisation de licences Libres et Open Source est-elle un
     catalyseur pour la création ou bien rajoute un niveau de complexité
     supplémentaire ?
   - Les limitations d'une licence peuvent-elles déclencher de nouvelles
     formes de créativité sous contraintes ?
  
  Nous sommes à la recherche de travaux et projets nouveaux et innovants
  d'art médiatique et de design, centrés sur le thème et les questions
  ci-dessus :
   - œuvres graphiques et installations
   - conférences
   - présentations de projets
   - démos de logiciel ou matériel
  
  Nous recherchons également des performances audiovisuelles qui se
  produiront dans le cadre des soirées du festival.
  
  Les projets proposés doivent répondre à ce thème et être réalisés en
  environnement libre et open source, cela concerne à la fois les
  dépendances optionnelles, les outils de production et le système
  d'exploitation. Nous vous demandons de publier les sources de votre
  projet sous une licence libre de votre choix ou bien de les mettre
  dans le domaine public.
  Les projets ne répondant pas à ces critères ne seront pas examinés.
  
  
  *Candidature*
  
  Le dossier de candidature et la liste des éléments additionnels requis sont
  disponibles à l'adresse :
  http://makeart.goto10.org/call/index.fr.html
  
  Date butoir : *samedi 31 juillet 2010*
  
  Toute candidature incomplète ou reçue hors délai ne sera pas traitée.
  
  
  *Calendrier*
  
  31 juillet 2010        – Date limite de réponse à l'appel à projet
  Début septembre        – Notification des projets sélectionnés
  4-7 novembre 2010      – make art 2010 - Poitiers (FR)
  
  Pour un aperçu des précédentes éditions, veuillez visiter les sites
  des éditions passées :
  http://makeart.goto10.org/
  
  make art est propulsé par GOTO10

  dear thomas,

  here you get a first preview for the make art design. unfortunately i
  did not have too much time to prepare, since we are arranging another
  edition of the "open circuit" in eindhoven right now. but i hope you get
  a impression.

  poster are set together from two main parts:
  the static part is generated with latex and holds information text,
  sponsor logos, etcpp.
  the variable part is put together from a collection of inkscape files.
  stored and arranged inside these inkscape files are graphic design
  elements, typography, illustrations, for title, logo, date, etcpp. A
  script produces variations of these source files AND we host the
  inkscape files in a subversion directory, so they can be edited by
  different people. by doing their designs people will help the archive of
  elements to grow. all elements can again be edited and modified by
  people and become again part of the final poster. we plan to finalize
  the repository structure and explanations asap and then start to invite
  people to participate.
  you can have a look at a source svg here:
  http://www.forkable.eu/generators/i-bd/i/TRUNK/LAFKON_100730--0-01.svg
  (download and open with inkscape)
  The sources are (ideally) a documentation of ideas and comments of the
  individual design processes, so they serve as connection point for
  different authors.

  here you can see some samples of rendered posters:
  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/makeart/100812_i-bd.zip

  these are just examples, since we did not prepare much source files,
  as we wanted to show you the tests first.

  for the sticker i think we can do a simple round sticker as we did for
  chmod+x. they were pretty nice and it should work out timewise.


  best regards,
  christoph

  Hello Christoph and Benjamin,

  ok many thanks for the preview.

  We discussed about it with the team and we've got some important comments.
  As I'm going almost offline for the next 2 weeks, here they are (sorry for the
  long message ;) :

  - we invited OSP to show Nancy for the exhibition of the festival. Obviously and
  unfortunately, you overlap each other there (focussing on collaborative font
  making processes).
  http://ospublish.constantvzw.org/nancy/
  It was a good idea to focus on this but you didn't know that it would be really
  too close to another artwork shown this year.
  Then well, we'd better have another theme for the poster.

  - generative process using different external components (free fonts all over the
  web, material etc..) to generate the logo is a good idea (but something different
  than last year obviously)

  - to avoid confusion, when I told you earlier that we'd like to have more polished
  work about fonts, I meant it would be nice to have cute fonts for the poster texts
  (the one used for the subtitle, the catchphrase, place, date, etc..). Cute as in
  different. Different than regular web-fonts for instance. hope you see what I mean

  - why not using colours this time (been 2 edition with b/w) ?
  After several internal discussions, we think it is time to switch back to colours.
  It can be black (and or grayscale) + 1 or 2 colours only. It can be a play with
  offsets/layers (punk style). Or something else.

  - Then depending if it's one poster or several different ones, it can be a matter
  of costs. So :
  option 1: If it's one poster, then we'd like to do it at a local printer where we
  could see the result, choose a nice paper etc... (Valentine from make art team
  will deal with that).
  option 2: If it's several/different posters/leaflets, please let us know if you
  know printers interesting prices regarding colours. Here in Poitiers we can't find
  any good digital printers who could do (except for the very big posters).
  Then, let's decide quickly if it's option 1 or 2.
  It could be mixed though, for instance you good make a different poster for each
  of the 23 big posters (120x176cm).
  Reminder: we will print 23 big ones and 6000 A3s posters. 5000 of the A3s will
  have be fold in 3 with detailed program/information at the verso (same recto though).

  - have you got another idea for a new make art "macaroon" this year ? It's already
  almost the same for 2009 edition and chmod +x art. Now moving on sounds a good idea.

  - minimal poster is the way. Keep some parts empty, light and smart etc...,
  minimal but efficient

  - Valentine (Cc'ed) will explain you how she see things about the A3 fold in 3.
  Also some ideas for listing the artists as we found the block text should be
  dropped this time.

  hope that's not too much, feel free to ask now if you've got questions

  Thanks

  all the best,

  Thomas

  dear thomas, dear valentine,

  i hope this email reaches someone before the offline period.

  regarding your worries about too much similarities with previous
  festivals, i must admit that we are wondering a bit, why you were
  actually asking us to do the job. Mostly anything we have ever done
  regarding posters, festivals and print was b/w and focussed on the
  experimentation on processes(and b/w is a framing given by the
  generative approach), not only make art editions but also the works for
  linux audio.

  If you had something completely new in mind, it would have been easier
  to ask someone, who does something completely different. The chances to
  get something with a certain quality, are much higher if you do not try
  to invent the wheel within three weeks. So it's not a bad idea, if there
  is already a direction or a fundament to build upon. But as far as we
  see it, our proposal is not really too close to last year. Actually it's
  pretty different, while pushing the theme forward.

  The parts that ARE close to previous edition, is actually the themes we
  are working on, where we try to develop something. This is the fundament
  we have, to do something within three weeks, where chances are high(er)
  that it is suitable for the make art festival, regarding quality and
  experimentation.
  What makes it very different, is that we move the generative process
  away from software to people, which by the way, is matching pretty well
  the collaboration theme. Your concerns about the parallels with OSP,
  which are, by the way, pretty marginal, because we do not really deal
  with font-making but font-using:
  Things like this will be really hard to prevent, because the world of
  (FLOSS) design is not big enough to not have parallels.

  Before i will get back to your questions, i will just mention, that for
  us it is really no problem, if you want to find someone different for
  the design. Probably it's not a bad idea to simply change after two
  editions (like last year) to get some fresh breeze into the thing.

  Because there is not much time anyway, i will pose some questions, so we
  can continue, if you do not have the opportunity to pick a different
  designer.

   > have you got another idea for a new make art "macaroon" this year ?
   > It's already almost the same for 2009 edition and chmod +x art.
   > Now moving on sounds a good idea.

  but the make art typography stays the same? because it already the same
  since the beginning.

  just to mention shortly, what you saw are PREVIEWS. principle behind
  the framework is, that is completely variable, only with the
  prerequisite of the vertical grid. so if one collaborateurs decides to
  do a different make art logo that's fine. we do not want to trim the
  design outcome, but just to give a minimal framework for collaboration
  and use this fieldtest as illustrative part for the posters.
  graphicwise this means that the identity for make art is becoming more
  unstable and fuzzy, than what you would normally see in graphic design.
  balancing this fuzziness in form with a certain recognizability is what
  interest us for this project.

   > to avoid confusion, when I told you earlier that we'd like to have
   > more polished work about fonts, I meant it would be nice to have
   > cute fonts for the poster texts (the one used for the subtitle, the
   > catchphrase, place, date, etc..). Cute as in different.
   > Different than regular web-fonts for instance. hope you see
   > what I mean

  i do not get completly the point about web-fonts. in this case we
  decided to choose the computer modern (which is LaTeX's standard font)
  to get a contrapoint (as IT IS a preset) to the pretty
  unordered/variable part in the top half. But I think it's possible and
  would be nice to get more detailed into the typesetting, but that's much
  work for the first draft preview.

   > why not using colours this time (been 2 edition with b/w) ?
   > After several internal discussions, we think it is time to switch back
   > to colours. It can be black (and or grayscale) + 1 or 2 colours only.
   > It can be a play with offsets/layers (punk style). Or something else.

  Unfortunately colours are a pretty hard one.
  If we want to have differing prints, which is more or less integral to
  the concept, colour printing is not really an option, unless you have a
  lot of money to spend. To bring colours to the b/w prints would be
  possible through paper colour (we sent you tests last year) or an adding
  a colour added after printing, e.g. through stamping or stickers. Or we
  could print the "hidden" grid as colour layer. All this, unfortunately,
  needs organisation what would be easier if someone would take over in
  poitiers (valentine?), so we do not have to send the stuff all over
  europe. And it costs more money, if we do not use the standard flyerwire
  poster printing, like anybody else. But it would be nice to solve this
  problem.


  looking forward to here from you,
  best regards,
  christoph

  --

    Christoph Haag

  > experimentation on processes(and b/w is a framing given by the
  > generative approach), not only make art editions but also the works for
  > linux audio.

  > to ask someone, who does something completely different. The chances to
  > get something with a certain quality, are much higher if you do not try
  > to invent the wheel within three weeks. So it's not a bad idea, if there
  > is already a direction or a fundament to build upon. But as far as we
  > see it, our proposal is not really too close to last year. Actually it's

  Hello Christoph,

  First of all good news about the new open circuits install, am I right
  to think that this is for the 'funware' exhibition?

  Regarding the make art design for this year's event, please allow me to
  insert myself in the discussion as I sense some growing
  miscommunication. To be short:

  - We like very much the 'in-between design' logo.

  - The process to make it, is close to OSP's work in the sense that it is
    a participatory typographic work. Remember that we would like to
  exhibit your process in the venue, which means that we need to find a
  way to put the focus, and communicate to a broad audience what is
  specific to your work. It would help to know for example, how many
  people you imagine will contribute to the work, how do you overcome the
  difficulty of using SVN for graphic designers and any other potential
  participants, can you think of a way to communicate the process in an
  exhibition context?

  - We do not want to have any other elements in the layout in order to
    keep it simple and put the emphasis on this logo. So this year we keep
  the communication to a bare minimum title/subtitle, make art logo and
  URL/dates/venue(s).

  - The make art logo, will remain the same but not necessarily as a disc,
    this is up to you. We just would like to have it not as big as on the
  preview, it should be just displayed as an indice, label, tag, etc, of
  the 'in-between design' logo, or elsewhere, your call.

  - We want to experiment with colours in the same fashion as you have
    been working so far, that is creative and DIY. Your suggestion to have
  color paper and ink is interesting, could you elaborate on that and show
  us samples if you have?

  We do appreciate the amount of work you are putting in this brief, and
  hope to not spoil the fun with our requests. I believe this is common
  practice that we can openly discuss about design issues and share our
  concerns and constraints with you, and that we will hopefully meet
  somewhere in the middle. Please correct me if I am wrong.

  Let us know what you think,
  Best,
  a.
  --
  http://su.kuri.mu

  dear aymeric, thomas, et.al.,

  > First of all good news about the new open circuits install, am I right
  > to think that this is for the 'funware' exhibition?

  yes. we will be in eindhoven right after make art.

  > - We like very much the 'in-between design' logo.

  thank you. since we got overlapping with osp's work anyway, we decided
  to stick to the logo, but to change the rest of the process, since we're
  running out of time to announce and plan the collaborative part with all
  it's difficulties.

  > - We do not want to have any other elements in the layout in order to
  >   keep it simple and put the emphasis on this logo. So this year we keep
  > the communication to a bare minimum title/subtitle, make art logo and
  > URL/dates/venue(s).

  so what we have right now is the 'in-between design' logo, constructed
  from variable parts, edited by the two of us. this logo and other
  ingredients for the poster are thrown into a layout engine based on a
  physics-engine.
  to realize the color part, we thought about printing certain parts, like
  a grid, in color at a online printing service (e.g.
  http://www.flyerwire.com/preisebestellen_FIPlakate.html?tl=PLA ) and use
  these prints again at a copy-shop to print the generative in b/w.. Since
  the online printer's are pretty cheap (ca. 230 for 5000 A3 posters) it
  should be affordable, if you find a copy-shop that will just charge the
  prints not the paper.
  we will try to send you previews the next days.
  i attached an early test, just to give you a raw idea.

  > - The make art logo, will remain the same but not necessarily as a disc,
  >   this is up to you. We just would like to have it not as big as on the
  > preview, it should be just displayed as an indice, label, tag, etc, of
  > the 'in-between design' logo, or elsewhere, your call.

  we'll try and keep you updated.
  is there somebody in poitiers taking care of the printing? because it
  would be much cheaper if we do not to send the stuff from here to there.

  > Valentine (Cc'ed) will explain you how she see things about the A3 fold
  > in 3. Also some ideas for listing the artists as we found the block text
  > should be dropped this time.

  could we here about the ideas for folding?


  best regards,
  christoph

      Dear Chistoph and Benjamin,

  Here are some pics of the programm-poster as we imagine it : it's a A3
  fold in 3 to get a A5 leaflet.

  We can use it both as a poster and as a programm. Indeed : on side is
  a poster and behind it's a programm. To fold it properly, you have to
  imagine it this way :
  1) fold the A3 on the  29,7 to have a 14,85
  2) then fold again on the 42 to have an A5
  ... not that easy to explain...maybe try it with an A3 paper to
  understand me...

  For the poster we don't really have ideas for the layout poster but we
  would like that the names and nationalities of the artists appeared on
  waterwork on all the poster : maybe one name by line.

  For the programm, the layout are just some ideas that you can
  change to get a global coherence. But the informations will be there.

  If the design of the poster is ok for the programm we can have the same on
  both sides but _the important part of the document_ is the recyo of the A5
  programm.


  Tell me what you think about all that,

  (keep Thomas as CC)

      Valentine

  hi Christoph, hi Benjamin,

  to make it short, yes we like it better like this.
  (however I'm curious why you don't use anymore the "in-between design" logo that
  was on the first i-bd.pdf sent (on 24/8). I thought it was an interesting direction)

  I could investigate if a local copy-printer would be ok to make it but I must say
  there are not that many able to realise custom requests in Poitiers (last year was
  easier process/concept). Also, need to find one ok to fold the leaflets.
  Do you know which paper choose to avoid "paper jam" at the copy-shop (when
  providing them the already colour printed posters). I guess using "mat" paper
  (instead of "glossy") will be better ?
  Flyerwire option looked interesting but unfortunately they don't ship to France...

  Actually the team here is very busy as we've got both a full time next to "make
  art", so we wouldn't mind letting you take care of the printing process in
  Germany. And we would cover all shipping and extra costs. Would you have enough
  time in the next few weeks to deal with this ?

  > when can you send the content?

  Being realistic, the texts won't be ready before the 3rd week of September.
  Everything should be ready by the 26th of September, hopefully earlier the same
  week as we've got a sort of text writing "sprint" on Monday 20th.

  Please let me know what you think.
  If you've got further questions, feel free to ask

  all the best,

  Thomas

  hi thomas,

  i asked a local printer and it'll be possible to do laser printing on
  a cheap offset print from flyerwire.etc.pp

  we did a test and we really like the combination of glossy color print
  and the velvet black from the laser printer, i attached some photos.
  we can take care of the printing here and we will send the stuff to france.

  how much would you like to print? flyerwire will cost about 80€ for 1000
  posters A3, the laser printer will charge 6ct per copy what will leave
  us with 120€ for 1000 posters front and back.
  So 1000 posters will cost about 200€ +shipping.

  Since this combination of laser+offset offers new possibilities we're
  working currently on some crazy color stuff, i will you update in the
  next days.

  can you give me already the information for the poster front like the
  participant names?

  best regards,
  christoph

  dear thomas,

  i was at the printer this morning since the boss wasn't there yesterday.

  - printing will cost for 11000 (5000 front+back,1000 front) 6ct each
     -> 660 € (+ flyeralarm coloroprints between 158€-200€)
  - they can just do folding in two what would cost 10€/1000 -> 60€
  - printing will take 2-3 days
  - how long the shipping to poitiers will take depends pretty
     much on the price

  best regards,
  christoph

  dear thomas,

  i think we have a slight communication problem.
  if you say:

   > to make it short, yes we like it better like this.

  we understand it more in the way 'we have had a lot of different
  opinions here, that would take too long to put them in an email, but to
  give you some information, we do not HATE it anymore'.

  but that's not exactly the GO-FOR-THIS-command, after we proposed a
  design draft. if you really want us to stick to/improve/finetune/upgrade
  a proposal, it would help, to be more clear or even lie and say: 'hey,
  we LOVE it. keep on going, but ... (change this or that)'.

  since benjamin and i had also different opinions and serious doubts
  about how and if this inkscape version would work designwise, we decided
  to go a different direction. A direction that is more clearly (as you
  requested initally, or aymeric 'keep it simple [... ]minimum
  title/subtitle, make art logo and URL/dates/venue(s)') and puts emphasis
  on the generative logo, since the inkscape-gui version was basically
  overloaded with all attempts we have tried since the start (generative
  logo + physics + color/black combination). from our point of view as
  designers we thought it'd be much better to skip some parts and
  concentrate/emphasize the others.

  just to let you know, also regarding the back-and-forth (because of the
  miscommunication), even if we decide for the lastest/current design, we
  probably have still about a week to work on it, finetune and make it
  really final.

  if we change back to the physics/inkscape version (and this will cost
  time), to prevent miscommunication and dissapointment, i just want to
  inform you that it is adaptation and reuse of code we wrote for a
  different project:
  http://fork.buerokitz.doesntexist.org/generators/va300/o/01/

  therefore we should really speed up the communication.
  what are your definitive deadlines?

  so far for the changed proposal. feel free to comment and we will try to
  figure the best out.

   > ok but it needs to be "fold in 4" (= 2 folds)
   > any clue about how to make it done ?

  there are companies doing this. that means after we get the stuff from
  the printer, we can send them to a folding company, what costs time and
  money.

   > by chance, any idea of price range ?

  acoording to flyerwire:

  A3 (~300x420mm)
  90 q/qm
  6000 Stück
  = 68 kg

  ->
  OPEXX: 220,- + U.St. (standard 2-days)
  UPS:   ca. 150,- aus, max. 70kg gewicht.

  (number is not updated to 5500, but this will be no significant changes)

   > it's nice basically, we find the layout
   > too similar to previous editions (chmod+x)
   > What about making a new css (almost) from scratch ?

  fonts/formatting are not superfinal, we just wanted to let you see
  something soon, but layout is more or less given. another possibility to
  have more significant changes would be to move the navigation from the
  vertical to the horizontal. makeart 2009 and chmod+x was similar, but
  for this draft i do not really see the problem. plus, as far as i see
  it, there is already a strong structure on the logical level (2 columns,
  navigation,...), so just rewriting the css from scratch would be
  senseless work.

  to be honest, i do see no real use in redoing the whole stuff
  just to prevent some similarity, since there is a limited number of ways
  to structure a website. yes, it could be done completely different, but
  to be honest we are lacking time for this at he moment. so if you find
  someone, who is willing to do so, feel free to pay him/her from the
  design budget.


  best regards,
  christoph

  hi Christoph/Benjamin,

  Thomas Vriet wrote:
   > Hi Christoph,
   >
   > I'm gonna give you our comments soon,
   > basically that's good !

  yes, I confirm, we all like it :)

  here are the few comments we've got :

  - the in-between logo doesn't really "stands out"
  maybe that's a matter of thickness of outline and/or adjustment about colours

  - the 2 logos (ibd and ma) are too close to each other and/or too similar size.
  What about having make art logo in black ? and/or smaller ?

  - the yellow is very similar to the one used by the "TAP", e.g. the big culture
  center in Poitiers (who eats all fundings... and doesn't care about us)
  http://www.tap-poitiers.com/
  http://www.mdapc.fr/wp-content/uploads/2010/04/tap.jpg
  http://cartedesressources.cndp.fr/intracrl/img/img_notices/4404_2.jpeg
  it is fondamentally not a problem but it is probably what people will have in mind
  at first glance. I dunno if it is worthing trying to tweak the colours etc... up
  to you.

  - about the white square
  at first we didn't like it but actually it's fine if this white space is used for
  all the logos (it can be a rectangle then..).
  And please put GOTO10 at the same level as the others.

  - on some posters, "Exposition" was not readable, it is important to have this
  word clean enough (like "Concerts", ...). No problem if an artist name is a little
  bit hidden.

  Now about the exact content, please use the latest .txt file attached.
  - the list of artists is up to date (dobereiner&morimoto are separate names,
  awkward not akward, simon and dorothé added, alberto is austrian, +oscar +xavi +stdin)
  - also we found a new catchphrase for the festival, putting it next to (below)
  make art logo should be ok. No need to put IBD subtitle.

  ok now you've got everything and you can finalize the poster.
  Let me know if I forgot something or if you need more details.

  about the website, claude will take care about everything, please just show us the
  latest version so that he can build it (considering you've got a few more tweaks).

  about the content of the poster verso (leaflet), we're late... but you don't need
  it for the 1st step (offset), right ?.

  Let us know when it's ready. Good luck

  best,

  Thomas

  hey Christoph,

  we had some feedback from an offset printer telling us that we should
  have a light layer for the offset step. Otherwise, the paper will be
  full already and won't absorb correctly more ink. In short they advise
  not to have a color 100% (whatever it is) where we're supposed to print.
  I'm not sure i explain it correctly, do you get the idea ?

  Also, i've been told glossy paper should not be used for such work.
  Problems may appear on paper with the heat of the laserprinter.
  So, mat paper is better.

  BTW, how is it going ? Any estimated time of arrival possible for the
  end of the week ?

  We're finalizing texts for the end of the week. We will pass you all the
  details for the verso then.

  best,

  Thomas

  layer)
  - we're not keen on the fonts used for titles (date, town, ..)

  unless you found a way to get the folding all in one quickly ?

  end of next week, 18th the latest.
  Is it realistic for you to produce the offset layer (corresponing CMJN PDF with
  right dimensions) on Friday morning ?

  Let us know.

  trigger the offset part soon ? How much time do you need to polish the b/w part
  and do the verso ?

  I'll give you more details about the type of length of paragraphs etc...

  hi thomas,

  > yes we're considering doing it ourselves since we're late already.
  > unless you found a way to get the folding all in one quickly ?
  > Basically, given the situation, we'd like to have everything ready to be
  > spread end of next week, 18th the latest.

  > Is it realistic for you to produce the offset layer (corresponing CMJN
  > PDF with right dimensions) on Friday morning ?

  we plan to send it out on friday(=tommorow) morning. if there are no
  changes the offset layer is already finished.

  we tried to figure out if it makes sense to do the production here.
  seems like the main problem is the shipping, since it will cost a lot of
  time and money. and because there are so many different people involded,
  the risk of delays is quite high.

  so here is what we can say right now.
  flyeralarm standard maximum quantity is 5000
  -> 4500 leaflets
  ->  500 posters

  ----------------------------------------------

  hello thomas,
  here the texts:


  ----------------------------------------------------

  LAFKON is a laboratory for graphic design occupied
  by Benjamin Stephan and Christoph Haag.
  Lately they have been doing practice-based research
  on generative processes as design tools and started
  to rebuild Deep Blue to become a layout intern.

  ----------------------------------------------------

  Inkscape meets the Bash meets Processing meets the
  *Philosophiae Naturalis Principia Mathematica*.
  In plaintext. Glyphs and graphics enter the wonderful
  world of physics to become posters for make art 2010.

  Thumbs up for Ricard Marxer and his Fisica and
  Geomerative libraries.
  ----------------------------------------------------

  best regards,
  christoph

  dear thomas,

  it was not easy to get big cmyk documents out of our current workflow,
  since we have to simulate the overprinting. what i can you provide with,
  is cmyk tiff images for the printer which should work fine.
  http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/makeart/101012_i-bd-bigposter.tar.gz

  you can download here a .tar.gz with pdfs and a script that you have to
  execute, to render the images, because each has a filesize of ~2gb and
  therefore it's too big to up/download. if your printer needs something
  different, the only solution i see so far (and also soon) is  to prepare
  the documents on a NON-gnu/linux workstation (we do have something like
  this ;)), since gnu/linux has still a problem supporting cmyk properly.
  it would be no problem to provide you with non-cmyk pdf documents.

  best regards,
  christoph

  ps: i decided to leave a white frame since i recognized last year and
  again on the photos that the panels are actually are a bit smaller and
  parts of the poster get hidden.

  Christoph Haag wrote:
  > dear thomas,
  >
  > it was not easy to get big cmyk documents out of our current workflow,
  > since we have to simulate the overprinting. what i can you provide with,
  > is cmyk tiff images for the printer which should work fine.
  > http://www.lafkon.net/exchange/makeart/101012_i-bd-bigposter.tar.gz
  >
  > you can download here a .tar.gz with pdfs and a script that you have to
  > execute, to render the images, because each has a filesize of ~2gb and
  > therefore it's too big to up/download. if your printer needs something
  > different, the only solution i see so far (and also soon) is  to prepare
  > the documents on a NON-gnu/linux workstation (we do have something like
  > this ;)), since gnu/linux has still a problem supporting cmyk properly.
  > it would be no problem to provide you with non-cmyk pdf documents.
  >
  > best regards,
  > christoph
  >
  > ps: i decided to leave a white frame since i recognized last year and
  > again on the photos that the panels are actually are a bit smaller and
  > parts of the poster get hidden.

  hello,

  so...
  first we couldn't view the posters with any software (gimp, gthumb,
  inkscape). So we can't check if it's ok here.

  despite of this valentine went to the printer to check if it's fine with a
  few tiff. Basically it's not fine... they had to convert to PDF, then the
  file was too big (300cm x ... or something)...

  basically, the printer really needs PDF files otherwise it takes much more
  time and cpu for them. They would prefer lighter files. He told us that
  150 dpi is enough if native format is 120x176.

  Other thing, the final file must be 120x176 no need to put white space all
  around (bleed area).

  hope you can fix this or propose something else quickly

  best,

  Thomas

  few more comments :

  - about the map, you can finally please remove the "église notre dame" markup.
  - also, would be nice that you put "(plan : openstreetmap.org)" in a corner of the
  page.
  - about highlighting the free parts of the festival, would be good to have
  something like an icon or a tiny logo to emphasize this in front everything except
  planetarium evening. And a caption somewhere else.
  => If you like, don't take into account the last .txt, these comments are in the
  .txt attached

  other thing, which is probablement obvious for everyone :
  on the current version, there are confusing overlaps between lines/texts etc...
  which makes some important details/information unreadable.
  That can be a matter of having a lighter map.
  but I suppose that's the next step in the leaflet design process

  cheers,

  Thomas

  hello,

  > what do you mean by
  > recto+verso version?

  they need a proper recto/verso file to start printing.
  To make it clear it means a PDF with :
  page 1 = recto 1st leaflet,
  page 2 = verso 1st leaflet
  ...
  page 10 = recto 6th leaflet
  ...
  page 101 = recto 51st leaflet
  page 102 = verso 51st leaflet

  back to the English print issue, I just realized that as the translation is not
  ready yet we need to postpone this cause we need the complete recto/verso files
  before starting. We will print that later. Hopefully it is proofread tonight but
  let's not count on it for now. I'll keep you informed.

   > do you want the pdfs with this numbers? normally i would have split the
   > pdfs to get moderate filesizes, e.g. 5 x 1040.

  It seems it takes ages cause the PDF are not flattened. Could you have
  produced such files ?

  And finally the printer only prints when the computer + the printer have
  processed the file. Although for all the jobs they do, it seems the
  printer start printing from the beginning.

  the test we did was :
  they launched the "300xenglish" at 13h15. The computer had finished
  flattening around 14h, then the printer was still processing the datas
  of the 100th at 15h. And nothing printed so far, I just called, the
  dashboard indicates "processing 293" (upon 300).

  the dude will finally use a faster printer (but poorest quality, still
  acceptable IMO) and use the same "520xfrench" PDF.

  best,
  Thomas

  hi thomas,

  it's kind of hard to really figure out without knowing too much about
  the printer and the actual problems.

  flattened pdfs are theoretically possible but they will increase in
  filesize, therefore i do not think that is really a solution to the
  problem :(.


  the easiest solution i currently can think of:

  - we skip the recto/verso setup (as in ONE pdf)
  - they print a 100(~)pages recto pdf and send it 52 times to the printer.
  - they turn over the staple by hand
  - and do the same with a verso pdf, e.g. 50(~) pages

  that way we would get rid of the pinterprocessing overhead. all
  solutions of actually modifiying the pdfs (like me trying to flatten or
  something) will cost too much time i think, because we have each to
  check back if it now works.

  did they try to print one of the real small files, e.g. 4 different pages?).


  best regards,
  christoph

  practical infos about their stay in Poitiers : few details

  the practical info)

  - to add the hotels + make more explicit Level6/GOTO10 address
  - reduce the map to the smaller rectangle (assuming it will be landscape)
  - make Gare, all venues listed and the streets highligthed
  - make the map readable walking-wise when printing on any regular black
  and white printer
  (- add in-between design logo)

  you can easily find the hotel address by searching in openstreetmap
  "39 rue Carnot, Poitiers"
  "35 place du Maréchal Leclerc, Poitiers"

  no hurry, but we'd like to send these details on Saturday.
  If you can't make it, please let me know

  thanks,

  Thomas

  dear thomas,

  making the map should workout.

  i attached a layout for the exhibition (it's arranged in a way that
  shows the 'progress' while adding the different layers). for the prints
  on white we would like to have the back of the offset prints, to have
  the same paper. for the sticking on the wall we want something that
  matches the nature of the posters as 'non-museum/gallery-artworks'. we
  do not know, what will be possible at the mda, but we thought of using a
  method that one would actually be used for temporary-outdoor-posters
  like glue (colle d'amidon?) or a staple gun (pistolet agrafeur?).

  christoph

  -------- Original Message --------
  Subject: make art - your stay in Poitiers
  Date: Sun, 31 Oct 2010 02:21:08 +0100
  From: Thomas Vriet <samoht@goto10.org>
  Organisation: GOTO10 - http://goto10.org
  CC: Antoine Augeard <traekam-noitcudorp@goto10.org>,  valentine dalancon
  <nocnalad.enitnelav@gmail.com>

  Hello everyone,

  some practical informations that might be useful for your stay in Poitiers soon.

  General
  =======
  here you can find a map of Poitiers, showing the main venues/locations :
  http://makeart.goto10.org/2010/misc/practical-makeart2010-guests.pdf
  addresses, phone numbers, hotels, schedule, meals etc... everything is there.
  Please print it.

  There you can find our phone numbers, let me remind them here:
  Thomas:  +33 (0) 671 073 691
  Antoine: +33 (0) 661 863 521

  Your arriving in Poitiers
  =========================
  For those among you arriving by flight, we will take you by car at the airport,
  please stay around and the driver will find you.

  For those arriving by train, once at Gare de Poitiers you're basically 1km by foot
  from the Maison de l'Architecture or 200m from Level6. If you don't mind walking
  there are some stairs or elevators if you follow the signs ("centre" or "hôtel de
  ville"). Depending on the time you arrive, please join us at Level6 or Maison de
  l'Architecture (check schedule / meals info on PDF linked above).

  Some of you need to quickly join a particular location (soundchecks for instance,
  heavy luggages etc...), we might have planned already to take you by car at the
  station and we will keep you informed shortly. If you think we forgot you or if
  you really need us to take you by car at the station, please just let us know, and
  we will send a driver/car.

  Sleeping
  ========
  Antoine will keep you informed shortly about the place where you will sleep.

  Meals
  =====
  served at 12h30 and 19h30
  as you can see in practical-makeart2010-guests.pdf,

  Your departure from Poitiers
  ============================
  the day you leave Poitiers, we can take you to the station if you like. Again, we
  might have already planned that for some of you who have got particular schedule.
  Please feel free to tell us if you need a driver.

  Strikes
  =======
  you probably know there are some strikes in France at the moment.
  If you meet any problem (hopefully you won't...) send us an SMS and we'll try to
  give you more details as the list of confirmed train is available online:
  http://www.infolignes.com/
  In the meantime, try to get information and to get the first train going to the
  right direction you could find.

  Your phone number
  =================
  please send us your mobile phone number if you've got any, that might be useful.

  Invoicing
  ========for those invoicing GOTO10, the following should be mentionned in your invoice :
  association GOTO10
  22 rue Thibaudeau
  86000 Poitiers
  France

  Important
  =========
  Please keep your tickets with you, we might ask you to send it to us back after
  the festival.
  Please keep know informed if you received your ticket (if you didn't do it yet).

  of course, more info about the festival available on http://makeart.goto10.org

  greetings,

  Thomas

  Hi everybody!

  For information, you will sleep at the Hôtel Central.

  For people who take metro :
  (plan of metro : http://www.ratp.info/picts/plans/pdf/reseaux/metro.pdf)

  * between Paris Nord and Paris Montparnasse
  You must take the metro line 4 (in purple on the map).

  * between Paris Est and Paris Montparnasse
  You must take the metro line 4 (in purple on the map).

  * between Paris Bercy and Paris Montparnasse
  You must take the metro line 6 (in green on the map).

  All these metro travels usually takes 30 or 40 minute.
  To buy metro tickets there are 2 solutions :
    - you can purchase tickets in some TGV lines (it's a better
  solution) at "wagon bar" or ask to the ticket inspector
    - otherwise, you purchase tickets at ticket offices or automatic
  ticket machines at metro entrances

  have a nice travel!

  Antoine

  I can eat anything meat or fish or veg, but I'm lactose intolerant, which
  means I have to stick to eating cheese and milk from goats and sheep (no
  cows).  I do love goat's cheese, and some hard cheeses from cow's milk don't
  seem to kill me that quickly.

  I don't want to make things difficult for you guys - as long as there isn't
  a huge amount of cow's milk and cheese in _every_ dish I should be ok.

  Best
  Evan

  > General
  > ======> here you can find a map of Poitiers, showing the main venues/locations :
  > http://makeart.goto10.org/2010/misc/practical-makeart2010-guests.pdf
  > addresses, phone numbers, hotels, schedule, meals etc... everything is
  > there.
  > Please print it.
  >
  > There you can find our phone numbers, let me remind them here:
  > Thomas:  +33 (0) 671 073 691
  > Antoine: +33 (0) 661 863 521
  >
  > Your arriving in Poitiers
  > ========================> For those among you arriving by flight, we will take you by car at the
  > airport,
  > please stay around and the driver will find you.
  >
  > For those arriving by train, once at Gare de Poitiers you're basically
  > 1km by foot
  > from the Maison de l'Architecture or 200m from Level6. If you don't mind
  > walking
  > there are some stairs or elevators if you follow the signs ("centre" or
  > "hôtel de
  > ville"). Depending on the time you arrive, please join us at Level6 or
  > Maison de
  > l'Architecture (check schedule / meals info on PDF linked above).
  >
  > Some of you need to quickly join a particular location (soundchecks for
  > instance,
  > heavy luggages etc...), we might have planned already to take you by car
  > at the
  > station and we will keep you informed shortly. If you think we forgot
  > you or if
  > you really need us to take you by car at the station, please just let us
  > know, and
  > we will send a driver/car.
  >
  > Sleeping
  > ========
  > Antoine will keep you informed shortly about the place where you will
  > sleep.
  >
  > Meals
  > =====
  > served at 12h30 and 19h30
  > as you can see in practical-makeart2010-guests.pdf,
  >
  > Your departure from Poitiers
  > ============================
  > the day you leave Poitiers, we can take you to the station if you like.
  > Again, we
  > might have already planned that for some of you who have got particular
  > schedule.
  > Please feel free to tell us if you need a driver.
  >
  > Strikes
  > =======
  > you probably know there are some strikes in France at the moment.
  > If you meet any problem (hopefully you won't...) send us an SMS and
  > we'll try to
  > give you more details as the list of confirmed train is available online:
  > http://www.infolignes.com/
  > In the meantime, try to get information and to get the first train going
  > to the
  > right direction you could find.
  >
  > Your phone number
  > =================
  > please send us your mobile phone number if you've got any, that might be
  > useful.
  >
  > Invoicing
  > =========
  > for those invoicing GOTO10, the following should be mentionned in your
  > invoice :
  > association GOTO10
  > 22 rue Thibaudeau
  > 86000 Poitiers
  > France
  >

  > =========
  > Please keep your tickets with you, we might ask you to send it to us

  > it yet).
